MEXICO
EnvirQnmental Proiect
Terms of Reference of Studies QnEnmc
Instruments for the Environment to bi CQmmissioned in 1922
I.   BAackgrou,nd
Before 1988, the federal government had the entire obligation -- or authority, to view it
from another perspective -- for correcting and preventing the negative effects of a development
style which gave no importance to the variable of environment. When the General Law on
Ecological Balance and Environmental Protection came out in that year, the responsibilities in
this area were modified to include the state and municipal governments, as well as the
participation of the private and social sectors. Citizen opinion has become more influential,
while the capacity for action has increased, as seen in recent years. The government has made
a growing economic effort, allocating already substantial resources to environmental protection
activities. With an important credit component, the federal expenditure, which includes
government-controlled industry, is close to 0.7% of the GDP in 1991. With the support of
private industry, Mexico already stands out for its interest in designing a model of development
which could be sustainable.
Now the federal govemment must go beyond its traditional role, wherein it took care of
all matters related to the protection of the environment. The resources required to meet a
challenge of these proportions call for a structure of sizeable proportions, which goes against
the current trend toward a reduction in the state apparatus. We need to evolve toward a unit
whose technical and political structure permits us to make a more effective response to the need
for continued growth, without destroying the possibilities of future generations.
The state and municipal governments, who are taking on responsibilities which have
always been considered to fall under federal jurisdiction, have to reorganize their
administrations. With the 21 state laws in this area that appeared before August 1991, these
governments are maldng the commitment to deal fully and effectively with local environmental
problems, and with those problems that are priorities for their communities.
Finally, members of our society can take on many of the tasks which today are handled
by the authorities. We ne-id to explore mechanisms of transformation, and of public and private
financial management, in order to provide incentives for community initiative which will
formally channel it into caring for natural resources and the quality of the environment.
For all of these reasons, the Mexico Environmental Project contains a special component
which explicitly links the problem of environmental management to the current economic



- 115 -
Annle& 2.3
page 2 of 14
framework in the country. Recently, a worling group was created, made up of high-level
officials in the Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology, the Secretariat of Finance and
Public Credit, and the Secretariat of Programming and Budget. The goal was to study the
interrelationships between economic policies and environmental policies. It was decided that this
group's initial work would be oriented toward answering three basic questions:
i)   How can the federal government ensure a constant flow of economic resources in keeping
with its responsibility to protect the environment?
ii)   How can the federal govemment ensure that there is consistency between economic and
environmental policies?
And, in relation to the above,
iii) How can the government use the instruments of economic policy, as well as other kinds,
to achieve the objectives of environmental policy?
In order to answer these questions, the Subsecretariat of Ecology needs to carry out five
lines of study on economic questions, related to environmental management and the utilization
of natural resources, which must be completed within a period of 12 to 14 months. Towards
this end, it is necessary to form a group of experts who can provide the Subsecretariat with the
studies described in these terms of reference. The working group will subsequently summarize
the results of these studies, in order to draw up a set of workable recommendations for the
respective Secretariats. In this way, the policy recommendations deemed necessary will be
formulated. Together with this activity, the working group will also define new research
programs, with a clear orientation toward management of the economic policies that should be
developed during the second, third, and fourth years of the project.   For these efforts the
worklng group will, as needed, seek the participation and collaboration of other entities from
the Mexican public sector, from the private sector, and from certain groups of prominent
researchers.
For the first year, the study program wilU be divided along the lines of the basic questions
mentioned above. The first three studies are related to the level of financing that can be
sustained in the ecology sector by the public and the private sector. The fourth and fifth
together are made up of a number of individual studies focusing on the effects of economic
policy on the environment. In addition, they are designed to look at the utilization of altemative
instruments which can internalize environmental costs as part of the economic decisions of
individual agents. As a result, these last studies will have to provide illustrative examples of
more general situations.
For each study, from one to four research groups will be invited to take charge of
execution. They will be asked to present proposals that conform to the corresponding terms of
reference. Given the clear economic orientation of the studies, it is particularly important for



- 116 -
Annex 2.3
page 3 of 14
the groups to include experts in economics (and/or financial analysis), or else to show that they
have specific plans to strengthen this line of activity through agreements with individuals or
other institutions of recognized ability.
A group known as the "Steering Committee" will be formed, and will include high level
representatives from the related secretariats, the private sector, research institutions, and social
groups. This committee will supervise the execution of the studies and evaluate both preliminary
and final results.
The specific details of each study will be spelled out in final form once the corresponding
proposals have been received, and the groups selected to carry out the studies.
II.   Descriptign ofLthe Terns of RefSrnce
1.    Financial analysis of the enviromnental sector at the level of the federal,
state, and municipal governments
a)    Objectives
The consultant needs to come up with the most precise possible evaluation of the public
sector's income and expenditures in relation to the environment. For this purpose, he will
evaluate current levels of expenditure in the govemmental agencies responsible for Saing care
of the environment. In addition, he will present recommendations regarding the budgetary level
that will allow these agencies to fulfill the responsibilities assigned to them under the law.
b)    Tasks to be carried out
The study will describe the duties assigned to the different agencies put in charge of the
environment at the level of the federal, state, and municipal governments; using those elements,
it will examine the financial and human resources they have been provided with. The allocation
of financial resources will be itemized to the extent possible. The consultant will define the
categories to be used, with the guidance of the Steering Committee. On the side of income, an
analysis will also be made of the various types of resources that have been generated by the
environmental sector itself, the quantities collected, the different sources of income, and the way
these funds are allocated. The study will assess how effective the different govemmental
agencies are in charging for their services. This will also provide a mear.s of evaluating possible
mechanisms for increasing the income of these agencies.
The study will focus on the federal and state levels; at the state level, work will be done
with two or three agencies so that they can be analyzed in detail Cramaulipas, Jalisco,
Quer6taro). Depending on the results obtained, the sample of states can be expanded at later
stages. At the municipal level, solely the problem of garbage collection will be examined, and
this only in a sample of urban municipalities. The data on garbage will be collected from the



- 117 -
A_nn
page 4 of 14
pilot project on decentralization in Tamaulipas, under the Mexico Environmental Project. In that
state, it has already been agreed to privatize most of the municipal waste collection and
management services.
c)    Program and information
The consultant will use the statistical infomation available on the accounts and personnel
of the federal environmental public sector, conducting interviews to get clarification and inputs
from the pertinent officials regarding specific points. At the state and municipal level, the
consultant should make use of the official accounts and payrolls available, with SEDUE support;
and when the information available is insufficient, he should, with SEDUE support, request
additional information through interviews with the relevant officials. The consultant should also
take advantage of the previous studies available, paying particular attention to the efforts already
made by the Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology. In addition, he will need to
propose a system for classifying ikicome and outlay which allows a consistent analysis of all
items; this will entail reviewing the systems of environmental accounts available at the
international level.
The study will have a total duration of 12 calendar months. The consultant will present
a preliminary progress rr'port three calendar months after project initiation. The report should
make it possible to asse s information availability, as well as the classification of income and
expenditures by item, and human resources by type; it should also give some idea of the amount
of detail that can be expected in the final product, particularly at the state and municipal levels.
The consultant will pre"iwt . second progress report seven calendar months after the study is
initiated, including a preliminary appraisal of at least the major categories of income and outlay,
as well as (classified) human resources, in the environmental sector and at the three levels
(federal, state, and municipal). On concluding the study, the consultant will present a final
report containing the expected information, along with an evaluation of the appropriate budgetary
levels required in order for the different levels to fulfill their legally assigned responsibilities,
comparing them with those actually exercised. This final report should be accompanied by a
brief executive report listing the principal conclusions and recommendations.
d)    Timetable
The study will begin in December 1991 and is to be concluded in December 1992.
2.    Spending and Income of the Non-environmental Public Sector for
Environmental Protection
a)    Objectives
With the support of the Secretariat of Programming and Budget, this study will define



- 118 -
AnDo2.2
page 5 of 14
expenditure on environmental protection by the rest of the public sector and, as applicable, the
sources of income that are available for this purpose. As above, it will be necessary to try to
come up witl recommendations regarding the appropriate levels of expenditure on environmental
control, as well as possible fiscal policies and their potential impact.
b)    Tasks to be carried out
Besides evaluating expenditure and income sources related to the environmental sector
in other entities of the public sector (as well as in the Secretariats of Agriculture and Hydraulic
Resources and of Tourism, among others), the study will look at companies in the semipublic
sector as well. In each of these cases, the policies followed in the area of environmental
protection will be assessed, along with the resources that are allocated to them.
Because of their contribution to the emission of pollutants, special emphasis will be
placed on those companies that operate in the petroleum, petrochemical, chemical, mining, iron
and steel, fertilizer, electrical power, and transportation sectors.
c)    Program and information
For the tasks involved in data collection, support will be provided by the Secretariat of
Programming and Budget, under the guidance of the Technical Committee for Implementation
of the National Development Plan for the Ecology Sector (COTEIP). The consultant will define
the expenditures and income allocated to environmental protection, as such, ahead of time, with
the help of these agencies and the Steering Committee. He will devise questionnaires to be
delivered to the companies in interviews, during which these concerns will also be discussed in
depth so that the most precise results possible can be achieved. The questionnaires will take into
account the inputs and suggestions of the Secretariat of Programming and Budget, COTEIP, and
the Steering Committee.
In addition to administering questionnaires, the consultant will have recourse to secondary
statistical sources, such as the accounts of the federal public sector itself, as well as the accounts
of semipublic companies. At the same time, he will complete a suivey of the literature and
studies available on the topic. He will also document the various operations of fiscal policy for
environmental applications and the possible results of its implementation, and will include an
analysis of examples from other countries that may be of interest.
The study will have a duration of 14 calendar months. Two calendar months after project
initiation, the consultant should present his proposal defining the expenditure and income that
are to be considered as income and outlay for environmental protection. By no later than four
months after project initiation, he will present his proposed questionnaire, together with a
progress report on the project. Nine months after the project begins, he will present a progress
report on the information collection, as well as on the administration and preliminary findings
of the questionnaires. This report should delineate some of the, mechanisms that could be



- 119 -
Annex 2.3
page 6 of 14
adopted in order to increase the resources available for environmental protection, and show how
these might best be implemented. The consultant will submit a final report 14 months after
project initiation which, in addition to providing the relevant information, will make
recommendations regarding appropriate levels of spending for control of the environment and
of fiscal policies and their potential impact. This final report will be accompanied by a brief
executive report containing the principal conclusions and recommendations.
d)    Timetable
The project will begin in December 1991 and conclude in February 1993.
3.    Private Sector Expenditure on Environmental Protection
a)    Objectives
With the goal of ascertaining the private sector's levels of investment in environmental
protection for those industries that are major polluters, and as a counterpart to the studies in the
public sector, the study in question will determine and evaluate the following for certain
industrial sectors considered to be critical from an economic and environmental standpoint:
i)    The levels of private sector expenditure on the preservation and control
of environmental quality;
ii)   the extent to which the companies comply with the legal provisions in
effect, as well as any related problems that occur;
iii)  the existence and effectiveness of any agreements that the companies have
made with the governmental agencies through different channels; and
iv)   the results achieved in the area of pollution reduction and environmental
control, through investments as well as other insttruments.
b)    Tasks to be carried out
The Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology will select certain sectors of activity
tbat have economic and environmental importance as the ones to be analyzed. In order to
address the above questions, it will be necessary, on the one hand, to devise a questionnaire that
specifically pinpoints these concemns, and on the other hand, to come up with a sample of the
principal industries and companies so that the questionnaire can be administered to them. The
questionnaiie will be reviewed by the Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology, COTEIP,
and the Stet-ing Committee.



- 120 -
Annex 2.3
page 7 of 14
Subsequently it will be necessary to visit the companies and conduct in-depth interviews
in order to find out how much they are spending on the environment, as well as to deteririne
the effectiveness of the technologies they have used in their productive processes. Meetings will
be held with the officials in charge of the General Directorate for the Prevention and Control
of Environmetntal Pollution to discuss their experience in this area and thus avoid duplication of
effort. Based on an analysis of the results obtained from the interviews, policy recommendations
will be presented to the workdng group.
c)    Program and informationi
Most of the information required for the study will be obtained through the administration
of questionnaires, as well as through direct interviews with officials in the companies that are
surveyed. However, the consultant will review the literature to find international points of
reference regarding levels of environmental expenditure in the selected industrial sectors, as well
as secondary sources of statistical information.  The consultant will need to specify the
categories to be considered as expenditures for environmental protection ahead of time, since
it will be important to get the comments of the Steering Committee.
The study will have a total duration of 15 calendar months. Once the items to be
considered as environmental expenditure have been defined, the consultant should devise the
questionnaire that will be administered to the sample of companies by no later than three
calendar months after project initiation. This questionnaire will be reviewed by the Steering
Committee and the Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology. When its contents have
been agreed upon, the questionnaire will be administered to a representative sample of
companies in the selected sectors. The sample design and questionnaire administration will be
the responsibility of the consultant chosen for that purpose. The consultant should present a
progress report containing the preliminary findings of the information collection seven months
after project initiation. An additional progress report should be presented 11 months after
project initiation, containing preliminary findings from the interviews conducted with the
companies in order to expand and refine the information obtained through the questionnaire.
Fifteen months after project initiation, the consultant will present a report containing the final
results of the study, including his policy recommendations. This final report should be
accompanied by an executive report giving the principal findings and recommendations of the
study.
d)    Timetable
The study will begin in January 1992, and is to be concluded in April 1993.
4.    Analysis of the Environmental Impact of Different Economic Policies
The fundamental purpose of the work included in this section is to make case studies



- 121 -
Annex zU
page 8 of 14
available on the impact of certain economic policies on the environment. Of the three studies
that are the subject of these terms of reference, two essentially have to do with policies
goveming the prices of niatural resources, while the third deals with the direct or indirect
application of the "polluter pays principle."  These studies will also present specific
recommendations, both with respect to the institutional framework, as well as to the economic
policies to be followed.
It needs to be kept in mind that, in conjunction with the studies described below, others
are being carried out, at times under the sponsorship of the World Bank itself, in the
metropolitan area of Mexico City. These last will also help to provide more elements for
judging the impact of economic policies on the environment.
4.1   Costs of the Health Effects of Water Pollution in the Valey of Mexico
a)    Objectives
Perhaps one of the principal economic costs of urban pollution is the impact that water
pollution has on the health of the residents. These health impacts can range in severity from
disease (morbidity) to death (mortality), in the extreme case. This study will examine the
information and literature available on the interaction between water pollution and health in
Mexico City. In addition, it will assess the relative importance of different types of water
pollutants in terms of morbidity and mortality. To the extent possible, the impacts will be
grouped according to location, age, and socioeconomic level. The information can subsequently
be used to establish priorities for the reduction of water pollution, defining both the activities
that need to be carried out, as well as the instruments needed for that purpose.
b)    Tasks to be carried out
An interdisciplinary team, made up of at least one economist and one specialist in public
health, will compile and analyze the secondary information available on the metropolitan area
of Mexico City. Attention will be focused on the health impacts of water pollntion and their
measurement, in both physical as well as economic terms.
The physical impacts will be analyzed utilizing standardized epidemiological approaches.
In certain cases, the individual pollutants can be identified, while in other cases more general
pollutien problems will have to be examined. Although the study will rely on information
available for the metropolitan area of Mexico City, in some cases it will be necessary to refer
to and incorporate the results of studies carried out in other places.
In addition to the information on the physical impacts and on contamination by pollutants,
to the extent possible, data will need to be presented on the economic costs of the health impacts
of water pollution. This should inc'ude information on the costs of medical care, loss of
productivity due to illness, and other variables. For the latter purpose, the documentation



- 122 -
Annex 2,3
page 9 of 14
available in Mexico City will be used, along with any representative findings from other urban
studies which include questions on the economic costs of health problems.
For the execution of the study, it will be necessary to rely on both an analysis of the
information available, as well as interviews with the appropriate health authorities. The costs
of water pollution will be presented in both physical and economic terms, as described above.
However, it is important to note that the study will not go into the economic costs of suffering
due to psychological disturbances.
c)    Program and information
The study will be based on secondary statistical data and information published in other
studies, as well as on interviews with the pertinent health authorities. It will have a duration of
11 calendar months. The consultant should present a progress report tlhree months after project
initiation. A second progress report, containing a description of the preliminary findings, is
expected eight months after project initiation, and the final report, 11 months after the study
begins. This final report should be accompanied by an executive report containing the principal
findings and recommendations of the study.
d)    Timetable
The study will begin in December 1991 and conclude in November 1992.
4.2   Fuel Prices, Intensity of Energy Use, and Fuel Substitution to Reduce
Pollution
a)    Objectives
The use of fuels and other energy sources in the economy is one of the principal causes
of pollution. Thus the management of political instruments that affect energy use can have a
decisive effect on pollution. In consequence, the principal objective of these studies is to explore
the prices at which the economy can decrease the rate of energy use, as well as to see how
businesses can substitute one type of fuel for another. This will provide a measure of the prices
at which pollution can be decreased, through the use of such policy instruments as pricing.
b)    Tasks to be carried out
When analyzing the impact of fuel utilization in the different sectors, the consultants will
need to be as specific as possible about each pollutant; inventories of emissions and the known
methodologies will be used.
When comparing the volumes of emissions, weights will be assigned to each of the



- 123 -
Annex 2.3
page 10 of 14
principal pollutants. The consultants will need to use the approaches previously employed in
other studies for selecting these weights, or else to conduct a sensitivity analysis.
The consultant will make use of time series analysis of the information gathered in order
to identify the principal determinants of the amount of energy use in the economy. If it is
judged necessary, the analysis will be extended to individual subsectors. The main interest will
be in determining the elasticity of prices, production, and other variables associated with the
various energy sources, as well as the principal substitutes for and supplements to these energy
inputs. Among other things, the sectoral breakdown will make it possible to analyze the way
that the economy responds, altering the allocation of the various fuels among sectors, or even
the process of substitution and conservation within each industry. The consultants will need to
pay special attention to demand response time in the face of the change in prices and production.
It will also be necessary to assess whether the possibilities for substitution and conservation of
energy are related to the age of capital equipment and thus to investments.
Subsequently, the study will make a more detailed analysis of the demand for fuel in a
few of the industries that utilize large amounts of energy. The industries in question include
producers of electrical energy, the iron and steel industry, the fertilizer industry, and the cement
industry. In the respective analysis, the consultants should use two different methodologies:
econometric estimation of parameters based on background information; and surveys to be used
at the level of the plant in order to collect technical or engineering information, based on
interviews with the managers and other industrial experts.
On the basis of the data drawn from the selected industries, the information can be
expanded to cover all of the sectors studied. The information should cover such aspects as the
type of equipment used, the processes, the levels of emission. and control. It is important to
remember that one of the objectives is to assess the possibility of substituting one fuel for
another; therefore the relative price structure needs to be analyzed.
The findings can be presented individually, both through the estimates of the empirical
variables, as well as through the results of the simulation models. Taken as a whole, the extent
to which a number of industries can substantially reduce pollution as a result of changes in fuel
prices would be an important input in the formulation of policy. The studies should also try to
quantify the implication of prices for the industries.
As in the previous case, there would need to be collaboration with both the Mexican
authorities as well as international experts in the execu'ion of the tasks described.
c)    Program and information
The study will be based principally on secondary statistit-al data and other (national and
international) studies previously published on the topic, as well . s on interviews with managers
and industrial experts aimed at gathering technical (engineering) information at the plant level.



- 124 _
Anno_2,
page 11 of 14
The project will have a duration of 14 months. The consultant should present a
preliminary progress report four months after the study begins, and a second progress report
eight months after its initiation. This second report should include preliminary findings on the
points mentioned in the first two paragraphs under section b) above ("Tasks to be carried out"),
as well as a status report on the remaining activities. Upon completing the study, the consultant
will prepare a final report. This final report should be accompanied by an executive report
containing the principal findings and recommendations of the study.
d)    Timetable
The study will begin in January 1992 and is to be concluded in March 1993.
S.    The Effects of Water Pricing Policies on Water Pollution and the Shrinking
of Underground Aquifers
a)    Objectives
Unquestionably, water management is one of Mexico's environmental problems. Due
to inappropriate population distribution in terms of the availability of aquifer resources, it should
be considered a priority to find a strategy for matching the demand for water with the supply,
so that water can be optimally allocated among a variety of competing uses. The extraction of
underground aquifers, and actual pollution (both on the surface and under the ground), is one
of the principal water administration problems in Mexico. And both problems have been
aggravated by pricing policies which clearly have long promoted misuse of this resource. Thus
the objective of this study is to assess, for specific localities, the extent to which such policies
have contributed to the shrinking of the underground aquifers and the contamination of this vital
liquid. The entry of salt water into the aquifers can also essentially be seen as a consequence
of water extraction practices.
b)    Tasks to be carried out
As can be inferred from the above, there will be two sides to this study: one part will
analyze the effects of water pricing policies on the shrinking of the underground aquifers; the
second will concentrate on the effects of both prices and dumping fees on water pollution.
In the first case, the consultants will need to make an inventory of the principal water
consumers, whether agricultural, industrial, or municipal. This information should be available
from the National Water Commission. Based on the information provided by the Commission,
the consultants should also identify or estimate the regeneration levels of the aquifers, so that
their capacit) for sustainable extraction can be determined.  It will also be necessary to
determine the pumping costs of water distribution, as well as the prices pl ;d by the various
consumers.



125 -
Aannea.
page 12 of 14
In order to discover the relationship between levels of consumption and prices, it will be
necessary to have a study of demand in each of three principal types of water users. This could
be difficult if the prices have been largely subsidized, as has been the case in many institutions,
including water supply in Mexico City. In consequence, the consultants will have to review the
existing studies on water demand in order to get an idea of price elasticity. Using this, it will
be possible to evaluate the consumption (and, as a result, water extraction) responses to
alternative pricing.
The supply of water in the valley of Mexico will be one of the cases under study. The
state of Baja California will also be examined, as a place where water is used fundamentally for
irrigation, and diverted from other uses. A third possibility for subsequent study would be the
state of Tamaulipas or the state of Sinaloa.
The second study will deal with the relationships between water prices and pollution of
the aquifers. Until recently, neither the Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology nor the
National Water Commissioni had established any fee for municipalities or industries to cover
their dumping of contaminated water. The absence of such fees, in conjunction with low water
prices, leaves both industry as well as the municipalities without any incentive for reducing their
discharges or for recycling the water they have already used.
Depending on its precise characteristics, the dumping fee could motivate these agents to
reduce both their total discharges as well as the pollutants they contain. It is foreseeable that
the polluters will control their emissions up to the point where their marginal control costs equal
the dumping fee. Thus, it is possible to motivate adequate levels of control. For this reason,
the consultants should also evaluate the structure of the schedule of fees that exists at this time,
the goal being to obtain material fof use in presenting recommendations.
In view of the fact that the study needs to be limited, it will focus on the basin of a
specific river. This could be part of the Lerma-Santiago basin, principally that section which
crosses the state of Jalisco. The study will attempt to estimate or identify the parameters
necessary to determine the "opdmum fee. " It is clear that such parameters are essentially the
pollution levels and their respective control costs.
In order to assess the efficiency of the dumping fee, it will be important to compare the
effectiveness of this instrument, which is based on market incentives, with the more traditional
control instruments currently used by the Secretariat of Urban Development and Ecology,
especially the 'direct negotiation' approach. The stipulated costs which would be incurred by
all polluting agents (undefined control of fees), together with the monitoring and administrative
costs of water quality (National Water Commission and Secretariat of Urban Development and
Ecology) should be compared with the costs incurred under the current regulatory scheme.
In any case, the decision as to the basin to be selected will depend on the infomnation
available; for this purpose, it will be necessary to consult with the National Water Commission.



- 126 --
Annex 2.3
page 13 of 14
c)    Program and information
The study will be based principally on secondary information sources, such as statistical
data and previously published studies. It will have a duration of 14 calendar months. The
consultant should present a preliminary progress report five calendar months after the study is
initiated, including the statistical information obtained and a description of the progress made
with each line of the study. The consultant will present a second progress report ten calendar
months after the study begins, with an update on what he feels could be the principal conclusions
up to that point, along with a detailed description of the tools employed and the specific findings
to date. Fourteen calendar months after the study is initiated, the consultant will present a final
report covering all the items addressed in sections a) and b) above ("Objectives" and "Tasks to
be carried out"). This final report should be accompanied by an executive report giving the
principal findings and recommendations of the study.
d)    Timetable
The study will begin in December 1991 and conclude in February 1993.
III.   The Conduct f theStudies
To make it possible to direct the progress of the studies, which are closely iinked with
the Subsecretariat of Ecology, a coordinator will be hired to coordinate this subcomponent on
economic mechanisms for protecting the environment, which in turn is part of the process
associated with strengthening of managerial capacity. With the Subsecretariat's Coordinator of
Advisors, who acts as the technical secretary of the working group, the forms of communication
that are most agreeable to the authorities from the three associated secretariats will be found.
The coordinator of the subcomponent will be helped by two experts:
i)    The person in charge of defining the legal framework associated with each of five
lines of study. His principal function will be to study the associated legal
ordinances, in order to be able to appropriately modulate the proposals that come
before the worldng group. In addition, he will prepare any modifications to the
current legal framework that are agreed upon in the worldng group. For this
effort, he will seek support from the General Directorate of Legal Affairs.
ii)    The person in charge of supplying technical and administrative support to
maintain the work of the persons in charge of the studies. His principal function
will be to maintain adequate ties with the Coordination of Advisors, and to
prepare any necessary documentation. He will be responsible for channelling the
administrative needs of those worldng in this subcomponent into the appropriate
channels where they can be addressed.



- 127 _
Annex 2.3
page 14 of 14
The study coordinator will have to maintain a close relationship with the Subsecretariat
in order to be able to observe the progress of the studies. According to a convenient schedule,
working sessions will be organized between the persons in charge of the studies and the
Secretariat officials who are connected with the studies.
Around June of 1992 a symposium will be organized on the environmental economy of
Mexico for a small group of participants. Experts will be invited from other countries, along
with researchers from the World Bank. The objective of this 3- to 4-day meeting will be to
assess the advances made. The progress of the Mexico Environmental Project, with regard to
the topics of economic interest, will be analyzed through presentations selected for that purpose.
The study coordinator will try to direct the work into the establishment of policies which
ensure that those who create pollution and/or degrade natural resources will be responsible for
paying the costs, which means repairing any damage they cause. The principle that "the polluter
is the one who pays" must be put into practice through the use of various instruments. Market
incentives are an important addition to motivate the allocation of more resources to the fight
against pollution and the prevention of irrational use of natural resources. It is important to
mention, in addition, the possibilities offered by the pilot decentralization projects. The persons
in charge of carrying out the studies that are the subject of these terms of reference need to take
this strategy into account.
The study coordinator will form a special committee made up of two well-known
researchers, two prominent business leaders, three SEDUE officials, and a spokesman for
environmental organizations which are recognized for their work in this field. This committee
will review the progress of the studies, collaborate in selecting the persons in charge, and
promote dissemination of the results obtained. The study coordinator will preside over this
group; its members will receive a symbolic payment for their collaboration.
As the results come in from the studies, the study coordinator, guided by the Steering
Committee, will be preparing a synthesis of the most important points. Three months after the
final study is concluded (in July 1993), the coordinator should present a document containing
the principal conclusions and recommendations of the studies, along with suggestions for new
studies that suggest themselves in light of the previous findings, so that these can be discussed
at a high level seminar or in other forums. This could facilitate translation of the study results
into concrete proposals for consideration in the process of policy formulation.

MEXICO
Environmental Project
Protected Areas Program
Eligibility Criteria For Supporting Protected Areas
1.   Each of the 17 areas selected for biodiversity protection would have to meet all of the following
criteria to be eligible for financing from the Global Environment Trust Fund (GET) under the
Environmental Project:
(A)   Non-availability of alternative funding for the activities proposed in the operating
plan;
(B)    In accordance with Article 98 of the General Ecology Law, the management and
operating plans should ensure that: (i) permitted land uses are compatible with the
specific characteristics of the soils affected and should not alter the equilibrium of the
protected area's ecosystems; (ii) >ermitted land uses should maintain the physical
integrity and the productive capacity of the soils of the protected area; and (iii)
permitted productive activities should avoid practices that would lead to erosion,
degradation, or modification of the topographic characteristics of the protected area
with consequent adverse environmental effects.
(C)   The area's management plan should have as a principal objective the
protection of Mexican biological diversity of global importance, with the
pursuit of sustainable development to the extent compatible with the
conservation of that biolog3cal diversity.
(D)   Preparation of management plans should be consistent with the strategy and
description of management plans contained in the document "Areas Naturales
Protegidas de Mexico: Legislacion y Programas de Manejo" (attached to this
memorandum as Annex 1).
2.   If a selected area meets the criteria listed above, the Bank will evaluate the corresponding
operating plan to determine the appropriate level of financing from the GET. Each operating plan
would set out the specific activities or investments required to implement the programs in the
management plan (including monitoring and evaluation activities). It would provide for the phasing in
of physical investments and investments in required staff so as to ensure the maximum effectiveness
of these staff. Each operating plan would also describe other activities financed from other sources
that contribute to achieving the objectives of the management plan. Finally, the operating plan would
contain cost estimates of all activities and investments to be financed under the protected areas
program.
